  <script>

    window.docCookies = {
      getItem: function (sKey) {
        if (!sKey) { return null; }
        return decodeURIComponent(document.cookie.replace(new RegExp("(?:(?:^|.*;)\\s*" + encodeURIComponent(sKey).replace(/[\-\.\+\*]/g, "\\$&") + "\\s*\\=\\s*([^;]*).*$)|^.*$"), "$1")) || null;
      },
      setItem: function (sKey, sValue, vEnd, sPath, sDomain, bSecure) {
        if (!sKey || /^(?:expires|max\-age|path|domain|secure)$/i.test(sKey)) { return false; }
        var sExpires = "";
        if (vEnd) {
          switch (vEnd.constructor) {
            case Number:
              sExpires = vEnd === Infinity ? "; expires=Fri, 31 Dec 9999 23:59:59 GMT" : "; max-age=" + vEnd;
              break;
            case String:
              sExpires = "; expires=" + vEnd;
              break;
            case Date:
              sExpires = "; expires=" + vEnd.toUTCString();
              break;
          }
        }
        document.cookie = encodeURIComponent(sKey) + "=" + encodeURIComponent(sValue) + sExpires + (sDomain ? "; domain=" + sDomain : "") + (sPath ? "; path=" + sPath : "") + (bSecure ? "; secure" : "");
        return true;
      },
      removeItem: function (sKey, sPath, sDomain) {
        if (!this.hasItem(sKey)) { return false; }
        document.cookie = encodeURIComponent(sKey) + "=; expires=Thu, 01 Jan 1970 00:00:00 GMT" + (sDomain ? "; domain=" + sDomain : "") + (sPath ? "; path=" + sPath : "");
        return true;
      },
      hasItem: function (sKey) {
        if (!sKey) { return false; }
        return (new RegExp("(?:^|;\\s*)" + encodeURIComponent(sKey).replace(/[\-\.\+\*]/g, "\\$&") + "\\s*\\=")).test(document.cookie);
      },
      keys: function () {
        var aKeys = document.cookie.replace(/((?:^|\s*;)[^\=]+)(?=;|$)|^\s*|\s*(?:\=[^;]*)?(?:\1|$)/g, "").split(/\s*(?:\=[^;]*)?;\s*/);
        for (var nLen = aKeys.length, nIdx = 0; nIdx < nLen; nIdx++) { aKeys[nIdx] = decodeURIComponent(aKeys[nIdx]); }
        return aKeys;
      }
    };

    window.identify = function() {
        analytics.identify();
    }
  </script>

   <script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
    $(document).ready(function(){
      // Hide Header on on scroll down
      var didScroll;
      var lastScrollTop = 0;
      var delta = 5;
      var headerHeight = $('header').outerHeight();
  
      $(window).scroll(function(event){
        didScroll = true;
      });
  
      setInterval(function() {
        if (didScroll) {
          hasScrolled();
          didScroll = false;
        }
      }, 250);
  
      function hasScrolled() {
        var st = $(this).scrollTop();
    
        // Make sure they scroll more than delta
        if(Math.abs(lastScrollTop - st) <= delta)
          return;
    
        // If they scrolled down and are past the navbar, add class .nav-up.
        // This is necessary so you never see what is "behind" the navbar.
        if (st > lastScrollTop && st > headerHeight){
          // Scroll Down
          $('.navigation__header').removeClass('header-down').addClass('header-up');
        } else {
          // Scroll Up
          if(st + $(window).height() < $(document).height()) {
            $('.navigation__header').removeClass('header-up').addClass('header-down');
          }
        }
    
        lastScrollTop = st;
      }
    });

    // Collapsable Search Field
    $('.search-field__holder.collapsed').on('click', function(e) {
      $(this).removeClass('collapsed').addClass('expanded').find('.search-field__input').focus();
    });

    $(document).on('touchstart', function() {
      documentClick = true;
    });
    $(document).on('touchmove', function() {
      documentClick = false;
    });

    $(document).on('click touchend', function (event) {
      if (event.type == 'click') documentClick = true;
      if (documentClick){
        if(!$(event.target).closest('.navigation__header .search-field__holder').length) {
          if($('.navigation__header .search-field__holder').hasClass('expanded')) {
            $('.navigation__header .search-field__holder').addClass('collapsed').removeClass('expanded');
          }
        }
      }
    })
  </script>

          <tr id="lesson-row-2547" class="lesson-row "> 
           <td class="cell cell-pseudo-checkbox"> <span class="pseudo-checkbox-holder"> <i id="completed-icon-2547-true" class="pseudo-checkbox" style="display: none"></i> <i id="uncompleted-icon-2547-true" class="pseudo-checkbox" style="display: none"></i> </span> <script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
                $(function() {
                  var completed = $('#completed-icon-2547-true'),
                      uncompleted = $('#uncompleted-icon-2547-true'),
                      tile = $('#lesson-tile-2547'),
                      row = $('#lesson-row-2547');

                  $("#lesson-row-2547 td").on("click", function(e) {
                    if( $(this).hasClass('cell-add-to') ) return;
                    if (e.isDefaultPrevented() || e.metaKey || e.ctrlKey || e.which === 2) {
                      return;
                    }
                    document.location = "https://egghead.io/lessons/implement-the-heap-data-structure-using-javascript";
                  });

                  completed.hide();
                  uncompleted.show();

                  completed.click(function(event) {
                    event.preventDefault();
                    event.stopImmediatePropagation();
                    completed.hide();
                    uncompleted.show();
                    row.removeClass('lesson-watched');
                    tile.removeClass('lesson-watched');
                    $.ajax({
                      type: "POST",
                      url: '/watch/manual_uncomplete',
                      data: {
                        lesson_view: {
                          lesson_id: 2547
                        }
                      },
                      dataType: "json"
                    })
                  });

                  uncompleted.click(function(event) {
                    event.preventDefault();
                    event.stopImmediatePropagation();
                    completed.show();
                    uncompleted.hide();
                    row.addClass('lesson-watched');
                    tile.addClass('lesson-watched');
                    $.ajax({
                      type: "POST",
                      url: '/watch/manual_complete',
                      data: {
                        lesson_view: {
                          lesson_id: 2547
                        }
                      },
                      dataType: "json"
                    })
                  });

           <div class="media-holder">

            <img src="https://dcv19h61vib2d.cloudfront.net/thumbs/egghead-implement-the-heap-data-structure-using-javascript/egghead-implement-the-heap-data-structure-using-javascript.jpg" alt="typescript tutorial about Implement the heap data structure using JavaScript" class="img-responsive"> 
           </div> </a> 
          <!-- video-holder --> 
          <div class="media-subscription-holder"> 
           <h4 class="title"> <span class="pseudo-checkbox-holder"> <i id="completed-icon-2547-false" class="pseudo-checkbox" style="display: none"></i> <i id="uncompleted-icon-2547-false" class="pseudo-checkbox" style="display: none"></i> </span> Implement the heap data structure using JavaScript </h4> 
           <div class="info-line"> 
            <small class="duration"><i class="icon-time"></i> 11:43</small> 
            <small class="folder"><i class="icon-folder-open-alt"></i> typescript</small> 
           </div> 
           <!-- info-line --> 
           <small class="description"><p>Heap is a data structure that can fundamentally change the performance of fairly common algorithms in Computer Science.</p> <p>The heap data structure is called a heap because it satisfies the heap property. The heap property states, that if P is a parent node of C, then the value of node P is less than the value of node C.</p> <p>In this lesson we discuss the key operations of the Heap data structure along with their performance. We then implement the data structure using TypeScript / JavaScript.</p> </small> 
          </div> 
          <!-- video-subscription-holder --> 
         </div>

           <h4 class="title"> <span class="pseudo-checkbox-holder"> <i id="completed-icon-2449-false" class="pseudo-checkbox" style="display: none"></i> <i id="uncompleted-icon-2449-false" class="pseudo-checkbox" style="display: none"></i> </span> Shuffle an array </h4> 
           <div class="info-line"> 
            <small class="duration"><i class="icon-time"></i> 3:58</small> 
            <small class="folder"><i class="icon-folder-open-alt"></i> typescript</small> 
            <small class="custom-label custom-label-red"><strong>PRO</strong></small> 
           </div> 
           <!-- info-line --> 
           <small class="description"><p>Shuffling is a common process used with randomizing the order for a deck of cards.<br> The key property for a perfect shuffle is that each item should have an equal probability to end up in any given index.</p> <p>In this lesson we discuss the concept behind the simple modern fisher yates shuffle and implement it in JavaScript / TypeScript.</p> </small>

           <h4 class="title"> <span class="pseudo-checkbox-holder"> <i id="completed-icon-2440-false" class="pseudo-checkbox" style="display: none"></i> <i id="uncompleted-icon-2440-false" class="pseudo-checkbox" style="display: none"></i> </span> Queue implementation using TypeScript </h4>

            <small class="custom-label custom-label-red"><strong>PRO</strong></small> 
           </div> 
           <!-- info-line --> 
           <small class="description"><p>A queue is an abstract data type that serves as a collection of elements, with two principal operations: enqueue, which adds an element to the collection, and dequeue, which removes the earliest added element. The order in which elements are dequeued is <code>First In First Out</code> aka. <code>FIFO</code>. The term <code>queue</code> takes it name from the real world queues e.g. "a queue at the ticket counter". </p> <p>A good target is to implement these operations with a time complexity of O(1). In this lesson we discuss how to implement it using JavaScript / TypeScript.</p> </small> 
          </div>

          <div class="media-subscription-holder"> 
           <h4 class="title"> <span class="pseudo-checkbox-holder"> <i id="completed-icon-1881-false" class="pseudo-checkbox" style="display: none"></i> <i id="uncompleted-icon-1881-false" class="pseudo-checkbox" style="display: none"></i> </span> Increase TypeScript's type safety with noImplicitAny </h4> 
           <div class="info-line"> 
            <small class="duration"><i class="icon-time"></i> 2:24</small> 
            <small class="folder"><i class="icon-folder-open-alt"></i> typescript</small> 
            <small class="custom-label custom-label-red"><strong>PRO</strong></small> 
           </div> 
           <!-- info-line --> 
           <small class="description"><p>TypeScript tries to infer as much about your code as it can.</p> <p>But sometimes there really is not enough context for it to infer reliably. If it tried to do such inference it would potentially result in more nuisance than help. So instead it infers the type <code>any</code>. This type can catch people off guard as it provides very little type safety. Fortunately TypeScript has a flag to make it easier to catch such unsafe code at development time.</p> </small>
